Jamison Brereton

34 (550)
All Gods (except Ahi 16, Ahi Budhnya 17a)
Vasiс╣гс╣нha Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi
25 verses: dvipad─Б 1тАУ21, triс╣гс╣нubh 22тАУ25
This loosely structured hymn intersperses verses relating to the sacrifice, especially its poetic portion (e.g., vss. 1, 4тАУ5, 8тАУ9), with verses dedicated to particular gods.

In the early parts of the hymn, the verses to gods are structured as riddles, and the god is not named: Indra in verse 3, Savitar in verse 4, Agni (?) in verse 7. But in later parts of the hymn the gods and divine forces are identified, starting with Varuс╣Зa in verses 10тАУ11. Minor gods predominate in this section (e.g., Ahi Budhnya, the Serpent of the Deep, vss. 16тАУ17), through verse 23. There are also several interludes requesting help against hostility and bodily harm (vss. 12тАУ13, 18тАУ19). The final two verses call on many of the major gods of the pantheon, without distinguishing characteristics.
There is a distinct watery theme running throughout the hymn, beginning with the waters themselves (vss. 2тАУ3). When Varuс╣Зa is mentioned (vss. 10тАУ11), it is in his association with waters, a mostly later quality of Varuс╣ЗaтАЩs. The Child of the Waters (Ap─Бm Nap─Бt, vs. 15) and the тАЬwater-bornтАЭ Serpent of the Deep (vss. 16тАУ17) con
tribute to this aqueous environment, and the waters themselves reappear in verse 23. The reason for this emphasis on water is not clear.

Jamison Brereton Notes

All Gods Renou characterizes this hymn as тАЬinvitation without praise.тАЭ The first 21 (or actually 20 and a half) vss. of this 25-vs. hymn are in Dvipad─Б meter. Despite its name, this meter should be considered to consist of four p─Бdas of 5 syllables each, since verbs located in the 6th syllable of a putative 10-syl. p─Бda are generally accented (see 3b, d, 4b, 6b, 20d); however, consider 14d, 17d, where verbs in that position are unaccented. Those two violations fall in the latter part of the Dvipad─Б portion and may be beginning the transition to Triс╣гс╣нubh, which takes over in the 2nd half of vs. 21. On the meter see Oldenberg, Prol. 95-98.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay pure and divine praise proceed from us (to the gods) like a swift well-constructed chariot.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let the gleaming divine inspired thought go forth from us,
well-fashioned like a prizewinning chariot.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda editionтАЩs resolution of the sandhi and accentuation of Saс╣Гhit─Б ┼Ыukra├нtu in p─Бda a as ┼Ыukra ├йtu is incorrect: the Pp rightly reads ┼Ыukr─Б╠Бetu.

The reference to the departure of our well-crafted man─лс╣г─Б╠Бis a fitting beginning to a hymn, as describing the dispatch of the praise hymn to the targeted divinities.

Griffith

MAY our divine and brilliant hymn go forth, like a swift chariot wrought and fashioned well.

Geldner

Die gl├дnzende g├╢ttliche Dichtung soll von uns hinausgehen, wohlgef├╝gt wie ein Streitwagen, der den Siegespreis gewinnt.

Grassmann

Das reine Sinnlied, тАУ das helle fahre, das wir gezimmert, тАУ gleich schnellem Wagen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe flowing waters having known the origin of earth and heaven; may they now hear (our praises).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Waters: an allusion perhaps to the subsequently received cosmogony, as in Manu, that water was the first ofcreated things

Jamison Brereton

They know the means of begetting of earth and of heaven;
the waters listen then, even as they flow.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner (n. 2a), flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa., takes the waters as subj. of vid├║с╕е and suggests that the point is that the waters are older even than Heaven and Earth: they are the Urelement.

They therefore were around for the creation of H+E and know all about it. In the absence of any other obvious subject, this seems reasonable.

In the 2nd hemistich the function and position of ├бdha are somewhat puzzling.

Klein (DGRV II.96 n. 23) lists it with passages with the тАЬlogical conjunctive valueтАЭ тАШthereforeтАЩ. But he does not tr. it or comment on its non-clause-init. position, and I find it difficult to wring a тАШthereforeтАЩ sense out of it. In the Prol. (369 n. 1) Oldenberg 43 suggests that the PB parallel (I.2.9, VI.6.17) with the reading adhaс╕е тАШbelowтАЩ is correct and the RV should be emended, but he essentially drops that idea in the Noten, remarking that RV ├бdha is тАЬtadellosтАЭ and that the emendation would also require altering the accent (to adh├бс╕е). Our passage is reminiscent of IV.17.10 ay├бс╣Г ┼Ыrс╣З╠е ve ├бdha j├бyann ut├б ghn├бn, which I tr. тАЬthis one is famed for conquering and smiting.тАЭ Both passages have a mid-clause ├бdha that introduces a pres. participle or participles and both contain a form of тИЪ┼Ыru. See comm. ad IV.17.10. In both cases I think ├бdha opens a mini-clause that modifies or expands on the main verb. In our passage I think the point is that, though rivers are very noisy when they flow (as is often emphasized in Vedic texts), these waters also know how to listen. Note also that in our case ├бdha is p─Бda-initial, though not clause-initial.

The waters listen as they flow along: they know the origin of heaven and earth.

English translation:

тАЬThe vast waters offer nourishment to Indra; fierce warriors (combating) with foes, glorify him.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The broad waters swell just for him;
they will be considered as powerful champions in the (battles against) obstacles.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the introductory remarks above, both p├нnvanta and m├бс╣Гsante are accented because they open 5-syl. p─Бdas.

Both Geldner and Renou take the (soma) sacrifice as the referent of asmai, contra both S─Бyaс╣Зa. and Oldenberg, who supply Indra instead. I definitely side with the latter. Like many All God hymns, the separate vss. can serve as little riddles, each pointing to a different god,, and the mention of vс╣Ыtr├йс╣гu тАШ(battles against) obstaclesтАЩ, even in the plural, seems a tip-off that Indra is lurking.

IтАЩm not quite sure what the subjunctive m├бс╣Гsante is meant to convey – perhaps that in times to come poets will talk about them that way in the accounts of the Vс╣Ыtra-slaying?

Yea, the broad waters swell their flood ior him: of him strong heroes think amid their foes.

Auch die Gew├дsser schwellen f├╝r es breit an. In den Vritrak├дmpfen sollen sie sich f├╝r gewaltige Herden halten.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYoke for him the horses of his chariot, the Indra is the wielder of the thunderbolt, the golden-armed.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Put the horses to the chariot-poles for him.
Golden-armed, he carries the mace like Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The 2nd pl. subj. of d├бdh─Бta is unspecified, but is probably the priests / poets associated with the current sacrifice, who were referred to in the 1st pl. asm├бt in vs. 1. See vss. 5-6, where this identification is more explicit.

Once again both Geldner and Renou take asmai as referring to the sacrifice. They also take the nominative(s) of the 2nd hemistich as coreferential with the subj. of the impv.

d├бdh─Бta in a: in other words, тАЬput the horses to the chariot pole, as Indra (does/did).тАЭ This seems unnec. OldenbergтАЩs view that the asmai refers to Savitar, who is then the subj.

of the 2nd hemistich, is far more plausible. Although h├нraс╣Зya-b─Бhu- is found only here in the RV, the very similar h├нraс╣Зya-p─Бс╣Зi- тАШhaving gold handsтАЩ is used a number of times of Savitar, and the uncompounded phrase b─Бh┼л╠БтАж hiraс╣Зy├бy─Б is used of SavitarтАЩs arms in nearby VII.45.2 (also VI.71.1, 5), as Oldenberg points out. Since Tvaс╣гс╣нar fashions the mace for Indra in I.32.2, calling him vajr├нn- here is perfectly sensible.

English translation:

тАЬProceed to the sacrifice like one who goes along the road; proceed of your own accord.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Set out on the sacrifice as if through the days.
Like a (chariot-)driver in flight, spur it on by yourself.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFrom the force of this (sacrifice) the sun rises; it sustains the burden (of the world) as (earth) supportsmany (beings).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

From its tempestuous force it has arisen like a radiant beam.
It bears its burden, like the earth its ground.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Like vss. 3 and 4, this contains an unaccented oblique form of ay├бm, in this case asya, and as with those vss., I think it likely that asya is the sign of a riddling mention of a god – in this case likely Agni, as Oldenberg tentatively suggests. Geldner and Renou also see a reference to the offering fire.

I do not understand the simile in the 2nd hemistich. If the bh┼л╠Бma that the earth bears is its surface, what would an equivalent burden be for the offering fire? In order to get 2 Dvipad─Б p─Бdas in the 2nd hemistich, we must read *pс╣Ыthv─л╠Бfor pс╣Ыthiv─л╠Б, as Oldenberg points out. Otherwise we have a Triс╣гс╣нubh anticipating the switch to Triс╣гс╣нubh that happens much later in the hymn.

Griffith

Up from his strength hath risen as ’twere a light: it bears the load as earth bears living things.

Geldner

Von seiner Sturmgewalt ging es wie ein Lichtstrahl aus; es tr├дgt die Last wie die Erde das Land.

Grassmann

Aus seinem Schnaufen тАУ erhob’s wie Glanz sich; wie Erde Wesen, тАУ so tr├дgt die Last er.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI invoke the gods, Agni, propitiating them by an inoffensive rite, I celebrate a pious act.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Inoffensive rite:ay─Бtuс╕е s─Бdhanс╣Ыtena: ay─Бtuс╕е = ay─Бtuna, an epithet of с╣Ыtena, ahiс╣Гsakena, yaj├▒ena, intending perhaps onewithout animal victims

Jamison Brereton

I invoke the gods without sorcery, o Agni.
Assuring its success through truth, I produce my insight.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Oldenberg asserts that ├бy─Бtu- is a determin. cmpd., not a bahuvr─лhi, thus тАШnonsorcererтАЩ rather than тАШnot having sorcery/sorcererтАЩ. The published translation reflects – and indeed reflects somewhat loosely – a bahuvr─лhi interpr., though I think the difference is minor. Renou also takes it as a b.v.: тАЬsans (user de) sorcellerieтАЭ (tr. EVP V), тАЬsans user de proc├йd├йs magiquesтАЭ (comm., EVP IV); see also Wh n. ad AV tr. VIII.4.16.

Nonetheless, a determin. interpr. is a reasonable alternative: тАЬI – no sorcerer – invoke the gods.тАЭ A 2nd RVic occurrence of this stem, acc. ├бy─Бtum in VII.104.16, with AV┼Ъ+P repetitions, is not registered in Grassmann, which omission is probably responsible for RenouтАЩs erroneously calling our occurrence a hapax in his comm. Unfortunately this other occurrence does not resolve the question of cmpd type. The cmpd. is not disc. in AiG.

Presumably the implied opposition in this vs. is between sorcery in the 1st half-vs. and truth (с╣Ыt├б-) of the 2nd half. So also Renou (comm.).

Griffith

Agni, no demon I invoke the Gods: by law completing it, I form a hymn.

Geldner

Ich rufe die G├╢tter, der ich kein Zauberer bin, o Agni. Ich mache ein Gedicht, es mit der Wahrheit vollendend.

Grassmann

Ich ruf’ die G├╢tter тАУ in Einfalt, Agni, im Rechte wandernd тАУ vollend’ ich Andacht.

Elizarenkova

Jamison Brereton Notes

Once again the unspecified 2nd pl. subj. should be the priests/poets.

Note the extreme alliteration of тАж dev─л╠Бс╣Г dh├нyaс╣Г dadhidhvam.

The morphological identity of this last form, dadhidhvam, can be queried. The three occurrences of this form are normally assigned to the perfect rather than the redupl. pres. (see esp. K├╝mmel 275), on the grounds that the -i-liaison is proper to the perfect. Yet no corresponding med. 2nd pl. impv. is built to the pres. stem; indeed, the posited correspondent (cf. Whitney, Grassmann ┬з668), the monstrous *dhaddhvam, is not attested in Vedic (as imperative, injunctive, or augmented imperfect). It is likely, therefore, that dadhidhvam serves as impv. to both pf. and redupl. pres., neutralizing the distinction between those T/A stems. In fact, given that in this passage it is parallel to the present impv. kс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam in the same vs. and immediately follows on 45 an unambiguous redupl. pres. form to the same root and with the same obj. (8d dh├нyaс╣Г dadh─Бmi, 9b dh├нyaс╣Г dadhidhvam), a present-stem interpr. is favored. On ambig. pf. impvs. see my 2018 тАЬThe Vedic Perfect ImperativeтАЭ (Fs. Lubotsky).

Jamison Brereton Notes
10-11 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

After several vss. with a ritual, priestly focus, we return to the semiriddling listing of gods, with these two vss. devoted to Varuс╣Зa. In 10 the subj.

Varuс╣Зa is withheld till the 2nd half, thereby producing a quickly solved riddle. Vs. 11 does not name him at all, but the referent is clear from the phraseology, as well as the previous vs. ### 10 The easiest thing to do with fem. gen. pl. ─Бs─Бm is to have it modify fem.

gen. pl. nad─л╠Бn─Бm, as Geldner and Renou do (e.g., тАЬde ces rivi├иresтАЭ). But it is unaccented and therefore should be a pronominal demonstrative, rather than an adjectival one. I therefore assume that it picks up the waters (─Б╠Бpaс╕е) earlier in the hymn (2c, 3a); the connection of Varuс╣Зa with the waters, though not as firm in the RV as it is later, would evoke them. The rivers are then in apposition to these unnamed waters. Renou in his comm. notes the тАЬlienтАЭ of ─Бs─Бm with ─Б╠Бpaс╕е earlier in the hymn but seems to stop short of syntactically separating ─Бs─Бm from the rivers in this vs. For further disc. see comm. ad I.68.7.

Jamison Brereton Notes
10-11 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

After several vss. with a ritual, priestly focus, we return to the semiriddling listing of gods, with these two vss. devoted to Varuс╣Зa. In 10 the subj.

Varuс╣Зa is withheld till the 2nd half, thereby producing a quickly solved riddle. Vs. 11 does not name him at all, but the referent is clear from the phraseology, as well as the previous vs. ### 10 The easiest thing to do with fem. gen. pl. ─Бs─Бm is to have it modify fem.

gen. pl. nad─л╠Бn─Бm, as Geldner and Renou do (e.g., тАЬde ces rivi├иresтАЭ). But it is unaccented and therefore should be a pronominal demonstrative, rather than an adjectival one. I therefore assume that it picks up the waters (─Б╠Бpaс╕е) earlier in the hymn (2c, 3a); the connection of Varuс╣Зa with the waters, though not as firm in the RV as it is later, would evoke them. The rivers are then in apposition to these unnamed waters. Renou in his comm. notes the тАЬlienтАЭ of ─Бs─Бm with ─Б╠Бpaс╕е earlier in the hymn but seems to stop short of syntactically separating ─Бs─Бm from the rivers in this vs. For further disc. see comm. ad I.68.7.

English translation:

тАЬProtect us, gods, among all people; render extinct the calumny of the malevolent.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Aid us amid all the clans;
render harmless the тАЬlaudтАЭ of him who wishes to scorn.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The hapax ├бdyu- has been variously analyzed and rendered: e.g., S─Бyaс╣Зa. ad─лpti- тАШnon-shiningтАЩ, reflected in GrassmannтАЩs тАШglanzlosтАЩ and probably RenouтАЩs тАШsans ├йclatтАЩ; Oldenberg тАШexcluded from heavenтАЩ. But GeldnerтАЩs (n. 12b) comparison of Oldenberg Avestan aidiiu- (YH 2x, plus a YA rep.) тАШharmlessтАЩ is surely correct and is accepted by EWA, etc. For disc., with earlier lit., see Narten, YH 280-81.

Our half-verse ├бdyuс╣Г kс╣Ыс╣Зota ┼Ы├бс╣Гsaс╣Г ninits├│с╕е is nearly identical to VII.25.2c ─Бr├й t├бс╣Г ┼Ы├бс╣Гsaс╣Г kс╣Ыс╣Зuhi ninits├│с╕е, though in a different meter (our two 5-syl. p─Бdas of Dvipad─Б versus Triс╣гс╣нubh). To accommodate the meter the verb and object had to be flipped and a different predicate supplied. This metrically driven modification procedure is instructive.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The 2nd pl. subjects of all the verbs but vy ├иtu in 13a must be the gods in general. The priests/poets who were previously unspecified 2nd pl. subjects do not command the powers to carry out the desires specified.

English translation:

тАЬMay the blazing (weapons) of foes pass by innocuous; separate, (gods), universally (from us) the sin ofour bodies.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let the unfriendly missile of the haters go wide.
Keep the infirmity of bodies away, off to the side. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The 2nd pl. subjects of all the verbs but vy ├иtu in 13a must be the gods in general. The priests/poets who were previously unspecified 2nd pl. subjects do not command the powers to carry out the desires specified.

Griffith

May the foes’ threatening arrow pass us by: may he put far from us our bodies’ sin.

Abseits soll das unheilvolle Gescho├Я der Feinde gehen; wehret nach allen Seiten den Schaden der Leiber ab!

Grassmann

Der Feinde schlimmes тАУ Geschoss entweiche; weithin vertreibet тАУ den Fehl der Leiber.

English translation:

тАЬMay Agni, the feeder on oblations, propitiated by our homage, protect us; to him has our praise beenaddressed.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Agni, the oblation-eater, has aided us with our acts of reverence. The dearest praise has been produced for him.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Initial injunc. 3rd sg. -iс╣г-aor. ├бv─лn (for ├бv─лt) matches the init. ├бviс╣гс╣нa (+u) of 12a, which I (and the standard tr.) take as a 2nd pl. -iс╣г-aor. impv. Renou takes ├бv─лt here as hortatory/imperatival (тАЬQuтАЩAgni favorise тАжтАЭ), but I see no problem in having a preterital (or perhaps general present тАЬAgni aids тАжтАЭ) injunc. form in this vs. characterizing an individual god. The 2nd pl. is found in the hortatory address to the gods in general, parallel to impv. kс╣Ыс╣Зota in 12c, whereas ├бv─лt is followed by an augmented pass. aor. adh─Бyi, expressing the reciprocal human action in response to the godтАЩs help. 46 The first half-vs. contains two exx. of -t/d ├а -n sandhi before nasal: (├бv─лt ├а) ├бv─лn no and (havy─Б╠Бd ├а) havy─Б╠Бn n├бmobhiс╕е. Renou renders the latter as if it were an acc. pl. to havy├б- (тАЬтАж favorise nos oblationsтАЭ), but this must be an example of a hasty Homeric nod, since havy├б- тАШoblationтАЩ is always neut.

Whose n├бmobhiс╕е? Geldner takes them as AgniтАЩs, which he offers to the gods. I think it more likely that it refers to our acts of reverence to Agni, to which he reciprocates by aiding us. So also Scarlatta (40: тАЬdurch {unsere} EhrerbietungenтАЭ). Renou takes n├бmobhiс╕е with the following clause: тАЬAvec hommages a ├йt├й d├йpos├йe тАж la louange тАжтАЭ). This avoids the problem and works well semantically, but in this hymn verses regularly fall into two clauses separated by the half-vs. boundary, and there are no examples of a portion of b adjoined to the clause of cd.

Griffith

Agni, oblation-cater, through our prayers aid us: to him our dearest laud is brought.

Geldner

Es helfe uns der Opferesser Agni mit seinen Huldigungen. Das angenehmste Loblied war f├╝r ihn gemacht.

Es helf uns Agni тАУ die Opfer essend, ihm ward geweihet тАУ das liebste Loblied.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGlorify along with the gods our friend, the grandson of the waters; may he be propitious to us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Along with the gods, make the Child of the Waters your companion. Let him be friendly to us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Here the 2nd pl. address appears to be to the priests/poets.

This is the one of the few vss. in which the half-vs. break does not coincide with a major syntactic break, and this is made more noticeable by the fact that there is a clause break between p─Бdas c and d.

Griffith

Accordant with the Gods choose for our Friend the Waters’ Child: may he be good to us.

Geldner

In Eintracht mit den G├╢ttern machet den Apam Napat euch zum Freunde, er soll uns g├╝nstig sein.

Grassmann

Macht euch zum Freunde тАУ den Sohn der Wasser vereint den G├╢ttern; тАУ er sei uns heilvoll.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI glorify with hymns the disperser of the clouds in the firmament; the water-born, sitting among thewaters of the rivers.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Disperser of the clouds: ahim gс╣Ыс╣З─лse budhne, dividing two words usually put together:ahirbudhna: m─Бgh─Бn─Бm─Бhant─Бram, the firmament, or the region in which the waters of rains are bound orretained, baddh─Б asmin dhс╣Ыt─Б ─Бpa viti vyutpatteс╕е (Nirukta. 10.44); in the next с╣Ыca the words are united as aname of Agni

Jamison Brereton

I will sing to the water-born serpent with hymns:
he is sitting in the depth of the rivers, in the dusky realms.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Assuming that it is the serpent that is sitting in the depths, that is, that the referent is Ahi Budhnya, who is found explicitly in vs. 17, I see no alternative to taking the nom. sg. pres. part. s─л╠Бdan as the predicate of a nominal sentence in cd, picking up the acc. obj. abj─Б╠Бm тАж├бhim in ab. S─Бyaс╣Зa. simply indicates that s─л╠Бdan is for acc. s─л╠Бdantam, and Geldner and Renou tr. cd as it if were a rel. cl. (e.g., тАЬqui si├иge тАжтАЭ), a translational choice that blurs the Sanskrit. The alternative, which unifies the syntax at the expense of the sense, is to take s─л╠Бdan as implicitly modifying the 1st sg. subj. of gс╣Ыс╣З─лс╣гe тАШI will singтАЩ in the first hemistich. So Scarlatta (134): тАЬтАж Den wassergeborenen Drachen preise ich тАж, {ihn}, der auf dem Grund der Fl├╝sse weilt, wenn ich im Finstern sitze,тАЭ construing c (budhn├й nad─л╠Бn─Бm) with the acc. serpent of ab and d (r├бjassu с╣г─л╠Бdan) with the 1st sg. subj. This interpr. seems highly unlikely: why would the poet тАЬIтАЭ be sitting in the darkness? and where does Scarlatta get the тАЬweiltтАЭ for the serpent? I do not understand the reason for the close sandhi of r├бjassu с╣г─л╠Бdan.

Griffith

With lauds I sing the Dragon born of floods: he sits beneath the streams in middle air.

English translation:

тАЬLet not Ahirbudhnya be disposed to work us harm; let not the sacrifice of the worshipper bedisregarded.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let Ahi Budhnya [/the Serpent of the Deep] not set us up for harm; let the sacrifice of him who seeks the truth not fail.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first half vs. is also found in V.41.16, and in both places it is metrically anomalous. Here it has the requisite 10 syllables for Dvipad─Б, but the caesura/p─Бda break comes after the 4th syllable, so that it does not fall into two 5-syl p─Бdas. In V.41.16 (which, with the following vs. 17, is metrically different from the Triс╣гс╣нubhs that make up the bulk of that hymn) it has 10 syllables, rather than the expected 11. It is also somewhat striking that two vss. in our hymn are devoted to the very minor divinity Ahi Budhnya, when far more important gods receive only one, and I wonder if 17 hasnтАЩt been inserted to make the identification of this divinity clearer, since vs. 16 does not give him his full title. It is worth noting that our 17cd was already flagged above as one of the few places in the hymn in which a verb beginning the d p─Бda is not accented. This may provide further support for the idea that the vs. is a later insertion. 47

English translation:

тАЬMay (the gods) bestow food upon our people; let foes contending for our riches perish.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And they have placed fame upon these men of ours.
Let them [=men] go forth for wealth, vaunting themselves over the
stranger.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The nom. pl. subjects of the two half vss. are different, in my opinion. The loc. тАШmenтАЩ, recipients of the fame bestowed on them by (presumably) gods in ab, are the ones who go forth for wealth in cd.

The phase ┼Ы├бrdhanto ary├бс╕е has an almost identical correspondent in nearby

Griffith

To these our heroes may they grant renown: may pious men march boldly on to wealth.

Geldner

Und sie m├╢gen diesen unseren Herren Ruhm bringen. Zu Reichtum sollen sie ausziehen, ├╝ber den hohen Herrn triumphierend.

Grassmann

Dass diesen M├дnnern тАУ sie Ruhm verleihn doch, und Gut erlangen тАУ die treuen Helden.

English translation:

тАЬLeaders of great armies, by the power of these (divinities), consume their foes, as he sun (scorches)the regions.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Of these divinities: eс╣г─Бm, of these; dev─Бn─Бm or marut─Бm, of these Maruts

Jamison Brereton

They scorch the rival, like the sun the worldsтАФ
those possessing great weapons with their onslaughts.

Jamison Brereton Notes

My tr. тАЬthe worldsтАЭ assumes that bh┼л╠Бm─Б is pl., contrary to the standard, who tr. тАЬthe earth.тАЭ I would be happy with the latter.

I have taken -sen─Б- as тАШweaponтАЩ here, but it could as well be тАШarmyтАЩ, with Geldner, Renou, etc. It does not affect the sense appreciably.

Griffith

Leading great hosts, with fierce attacks of these, they burn their foes as the Sun burns the earth.

Geldner

Sie machen dem Feinde hei├Я wie die Sonne den Erdboden, mit ihrem Ungest├╝m in gro├Яer Heerschar.

Grassmann

Den Feind erhitzen, тАУ wie Glut die Erde, die Heer umscharten тАУ mit ihren Schrecken.

English translation:

тАЬWhen the wives (of the gods) come before us, may the dextrous Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б grant us male progeny.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When the Wives (of the Gods) will come to us,
let Tvaс╣гс╣нar of the lovely hands confer heroes (on us).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The pl. тАЬwivesтАЭ (p├бtn─лс╕е), as often in the RV, must refer to the Wives of the Gods. As I have argued elsewhere (тАЬтАШSacrificer’s WifeтАЩ in the Rig Veda: Ritual Innovation?тАЭ 2018 in Proceedings of the 13th World Skt. Conf., 2006), one of the models for the introduction of the SacrificerтАЩs Wife (p├бtn─л) in Vedic ritual, beginning in the late RV, is the presence of the Wives of the Gods on the ritual ground, as here.

Tvaс╣гс╣нar is their usual companion and chaperone. He is also associated with the shaping of the embryo in the womb, as in the pregnancy charm X.184.1. The request that he confer heroes on us here must be a prayer for sons (who will become) heroes.

Griffith

What time our wives draw near to us, may he, left-handed Tvastar, give us hero sons.

Geldner

Wenn die Gattinnen zu uns kommen werden, so soll Tvastri mit den geschickten H├дnden uns S├╢hne schaffen.

Grassmann

Wenn unsre Weiber тАУ mit uns sich paaren, dann geb uns Tvaschtar, тАУ der K├╝nstler, S├╢hne.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬMay Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б be propitiated by this our praise; may he who is of comprehensive understanding beinclined to give us wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Might Tvaс╣гс╣нar enjoy our praise.
Might Aramati [/Devotion], seeking goods, be in us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted above, the first hemistich contains 10 syllables falling into two 5-syllable p─Бdas, but the second half is a straight Triс╣гс╣нubh, anticipating the Triс╣гс╣нubhs of the rest of the hymn.

The stem vas┼лy├║- can modify both masc. and, as here, fem. nouns. This exact phrase, ar├бmatir vas┼лy├║с╕е is also found at VII.1.6.

May Tvastar find our hymn acceptable, and may Aramati, seeking wealth, be ours.

Es nehme Tvaschtar тАУ das Lob entgegen, die Andachtsg├╢ttin sei reich an Gut, uns.

Jamison Brereton

The Gift-Escorts will give goods to us. Let Rodas─л, let Varuс╣З─Бс╣З─л pay heed.
Let him be one affording good shelter (along?) with the Shielding
Goddesses; let generously giving Tvaс╣гс╣нar apportion wealth.

Griffith

May they who lavish gifts bestow those treasures: may Rodasi and Varunani listen.
May he, with the Varutris, be our refuge, may bountiful Tvastar give us store of riches.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рддрд╛) рддрд╛рдирд┐ (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН (рд░рд╛рд╕рдиреН) рдкреНрд░рджрджреНрдпреБрдГ (рд░рд╛рддрд┐рд╖рд╛рдЪрдГ) рдпреЗ рд░рд╛рддрд┐рдВ рд╕рдЪрдиреНрддреЗ рд╕рдореНрдмрдзреНрдирдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ (рд╡рд╕реВрдирд┐) рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ (рдЖ) (рд░реЛрджрд╕реА) рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпреМ (рд╡рд░реБрдгрд╛рдиреА) рдЬрд▓рд╛рджрд┐рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердпреБрдХреНрддреЗ (рд╢реГрдгреЛрддреБ) (рд╡рд░реВрддреНрд░реАрднрд┐рдГ) рд╡рд░рдгреАрдпрд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рднрд┐рдГ (рд╕реБрд╢рд░рдгрдГ) рд╢реЛрднрдирдВ рд╢рд░рдгрдорд╛рд╢реНрд░рдпреЛ рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдГ (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН (рдЕрд╕реНрддреБ) (рддреНрд╡рд╖реНрдЯрд╛) рджреБрдГрдЦрд╡рд┐рдЪреНрдЫреЗрджрдХрдГ (рд╕реБрджрддреНрд░рдГ) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрджрд╛рдирдГ (рд╡рд┐, рджрдзрд╛рддреБ) (рд░рд╛рдпрдГ) рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ реереиреирее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the mountains, the waters, the liberal (wives of the gods), the plural nts, also the heaven and theearth, consentient with the forest lords and both the heaven and earth, preserve for us those (coveted) riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Then let the mountains (apportion) us wealth, then let the waters, then the Gift-Escorts, the plants, and Heaven,
and Earth jointly with the trees. The two world-halves will protect us all around.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Both Geldner and Renou take r─Б╠Бyaс╕е here as nom. sg., parallel to the other entities like mountains and waters, but I do not see why the construction that ends vs. 22, v├н dadh─Бtu r─Б╠Бyaс╕е тАЬlet him apportion wealth,тАЭ is not simply continued here. There r─Б╠Бyaс╕е must be the obj. of the verb, whether acc. pl. or partitive gen. sg.; in either case the preferred accent would be r─Бy├бс╕е, but there are enough forms with the opposite accent that we need not be too troubled. If we can accept the wrong accent in 22d, I see no reason not to do so in 23a. Renou gestures towards my interpr. in his n.

Griffith

So may rich Mountains and the liberal Waters, so may all Herbs that grow on ground, and Heaven,
And Earth accordant with the Forest-Sovrans, and both the World-halves round about protect us.

Geldner

Das sollen uns die Reicht├╝mer, die Berge, das sollen uns die Gew├дsser, das die Ratisac┬┤s, die Pflanzen und der Himmel, die Erde im Verein mit den B├дumen gew├дhren, beide Rodasi m├╢gen uns ringsum sch├╝tzen.

Grassmann

Das m├╢gen uns die Reichen geben, die Berge, das die Wasser, das die Spenderinnen, die Kr├дuter und der Himmel, die Erde vereinigt mit den B├дumen; die beiden Welten m├╢gen uns beschirmen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet the vast heaven and earth consent, let the brilliant Varuс╣Зa, of whom Indra is the friend consent; letall the victorious Maruts consent that we may be a recepacle for the retention of riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Then let the two broad world-halves follow suit, let heaven-ruling Varuс╣Зa, whose comrade is Indra, follow;
let all the Maruts, who are victorious, follow. Might we be (fit) to found the buttress of wealth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the izafe-like y├й sah─Б╠Бsaс╕е nominal relative clause.

Correctly accented gen. sg. r─Бy├бс╕е appears here; see comm. on vss. 22-23.

On the infinitive construction here, see Keydana, Infinitive im с╣Ъgveda, 70, 159.

Griffith

To this may both the wide Worlds lend approval, and Varuna in heaven, whose Friend is Indra.
May all the Maruts give consent, the Victors, that we may hold great wealth in firm possession.

Geldner

Dem sollen die weiten Rodasi stattgeben, dem der himmlische Varuna, der Indra zum Freunde hat, dem alle Marut, die gewaltigen. Wir m├╢chten imstande sein, die Grundlage des Reichtums zu legen.

Grassmann

Das m├╢gen beide Welten uns gew├дhren, das der himmlische Varuna, des Indra Genosse, das alle Maruts, die gewaltigen, dass festen Grund des Reichthums wir erlangen.

Elizarenkova

тАЬMay Indra, Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, Agni, the waters, the herbs, the trees, be plural ased by our (praise); may we,(reclining) on the lap of the Maruts, enjoy felicity; and do you ever cherish us with blessings.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Indra, Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, Agni, the waters, the plants, the trees shall enjoy this of ours.
Might we be in the shelter, in the lap of the Maruts. тАУ Do you protect us always with your blessings.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not understand why Geldner and Renou render the juс╣гanta, to the common and well-understood medial stem juс╣г├бte тАШenjoysтАЩ, as тАШgrantтАЩ (zibilligen) and тАШagreeтАЩ 48 respectively. Although it is true that the final vss. of hymns frequently ask gods for things, it is also true that we commend our praises to them – and surely thatтАЩs whatтАЩs going on here: we want the gods to take pleasure in the hymn, or the ritual in general, that we have just offered them.

May we find refuge in the Marut’s bosom. Protect us evermore, ye Gods, with blessings.

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдРрд╕реА рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛ рдХрд░рдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рдХрд┐ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧ рд╕реЗ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдмрд┐рдЬреБрд▓реА рдЖрджрд┐ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрде рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдХрд╛рдореЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╕реЗрд╡реЗрдВ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рди рдХрд░реЗрдВ реереирелрее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдЕрдзреНрдпреЗрддрд╛, рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ, рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА, рдкреБрд░реБрд╖, рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛, рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛, рд╕реЗрдирд╛, рднреГрддреНрдп рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрджреЗрд╡реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг рдФрд░ рдХрд░реНрдореЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдЗрд╕рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдЪреМрдВрддреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рд╕рддреНрддрд╛рдИрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛ ! рдпреЗ рд╡рдирд┐рди рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░реЛ рд╡рд░реБрдгреЛ рдорд┐рддреНрд░реЛрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рд╛рдк рдУрд╖рдзреАрд╢реНрдЪ рдирд╕реНрддрдЮреНрдЬреБрд╖рдиреНрдд рдпреЗрди рдпреВрдпрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрдирдГ рд╕рджрд╛ рдкрд╛рдд рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдпреБрд╖реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдорд░реБрддрд╛рдореБрдкрд╕реНрдереЗ рд╢рд░реНрдордиреН рд╡рдпрдВ рд╕реНрдерд┐рд░рд╛рдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо реереирелрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕реЗрд╡реНрдпрд╕реЗрд╡рдХрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХрд╛рдзреНрдпреЗрддрд╛рд░рдГ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдВ рдХрдердВ рд╡рд░реНрддреЗрд░рдиреНрдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рддрддреН) рд╕реБрдЦрдореН (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджрд┐рд╡ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ (рд╡рд░реБрдгрдГ) рд╢реНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдардГ (рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдГ) рд╕рдЦрд╛ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рдкрд╛рд╡рдХрдГ (рдЖрдкрдГ) рдЬрд▓рд╛рдирд┐ (рдУрд╖рдзреАрдГ) рдпрд╡рд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдГ (рд╡рдирд┐рдирдГ) рдХрд┐рд░рдгрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ (рдЬреБрд╖рдиреНрдд) рд╕реЗрд╡рдиреНрддреЗ (рд╢рд░реНрдордиреН) рд╢рд░реНрдордгрд┐ рд╕реБрдЦреЗ рдЧреГрд╣реЗ рд╡рд╛ (рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо) рднрд╡реЗрдо (рдорд░реБрддрд╛рдореН) рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдореН (рдЙрдкрд╕реНрдереЗ) рд╕рдореАрдкреЗ (рдпреВрдпрдореН) (рдкрд╛рдд) (рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ (рд╕рджрд╛) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН реереирелрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреИрд░рд┐рджрдореЗрд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреЗрди рдпрдерд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рджрдпрдГ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рд╕реНрд╕реНрд╡рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╛рдгрд┐ рд╕реЗрд╡реЗрд░рдиреН рддрдерд╛ рд╡рдпрдордиреБ рддрд┐рд╖реНрдареЗрдореЗрддрд┐ реереирелрее рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рдзреНрдпреЗрддреНрд░рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХрд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╕реЗрдирд╛рднреГрддреНрдпрд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗрджреЗрд╡рдЧреБрдгрдХреГрддреНрдпрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрддреБрд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╕рдкреНрддрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ
